10.1.5  Conclusions for Phase I Chemical Analyses 
 

Results from the drilling and testing work completed by Eramine are considered to be 

favorable for the Project. Although wells were drilled less than about 150 meters depth, brine 

was evident throughout the entire section drilled, and suggested that brine values extend deeper 

than 150 meters. Lithium values are fairly constant between the pumping tests and drilling 

samples. The overall lithium grades range from about 330-560 mg/L.  It is typical to encounter 

more dense brine and higher lithium concentration at greater depths, as the denser brine tends 

to sink over time. Of greater significance is the brine quality. The basic chemical relationship 

indicative of lithium brine quality is the ratio of magnesium to lithium (Mg:Li) of 5.35 - 7.87.  

A drill hole summary of these ratios is presented in Table 10.5.  

 

Table 10.5.  Summary of Chemistry Results for Selected Phase I Wells

10.2  PHASE  II FIELD ACTIVITIES 
 

 The following section documents the recently-completed Phase II exploration field 

activities. Montgomery & Associates has supported Millennial for these activities both in the 

field and from their base in Santiago, Chile.  The Phase II exploration program was designed 

to develop a resource estimate, and also to demonstrate that large amounts of brine can be 

pumped from the salar to eventually support development of a lithium brine extraction project.  

Results of the pumping test have been included in this section.  Locations for all Millennial 

completed and abandoned boreholes and exploration wells as of November 30, 2017 are shown 

on Figure 9.9. Results from the Phase II drilling and testing program being reported include 

the following: 

 

• Diamond drilling program (Coreholes PGMW16-01 through PGMW17-10) (Figures 
B-1 through B-20), 

• Mud rotary well PGMW17-11 (Figure B-21), 
• Construction of brine exploration well PGPW16-01 (Figure B-22), 
• Pumping test for brine exploration well PGPW16-01 (Appendix C), and 
• Borehole electrical conductivity profiles (Appendix D). 

 

10.2.1  Diamond Drilling and Mud Rotary Program  
 

The diamond drilling program included drilling 22 vertical coreholes or wells ranging 

in depth from 154 to 601 meters (Figure 9.9). The drilling contractor was Hidrotec S.R.L., 

headquartered in Salta, Argentina.  The following represents a brief summary of the equipment 

and methods utilized. 

 

• For each drill core, recovery percentage is recorded 
• Core is described and stored in labeled cardboard core boxes 
• When drilling changes to rotary drilling, drill cuttings are collected, described, and 

stored in cuttings boxes 
• Once drill operation is completed, 2-inch schedule 80 PVC, and Slot-40 (1 mm) PVC 

screen is installed in the well  
 

Current location and sample information for all coreholes are given in Table 10.6.  

Preliminary schematic diagrams for coreholes and pumping well PGPW16-01, together with

(Appendix B).  Laboratory analytical results for the drainable porosity samples are given in 

Appendices E and F.

Most of the wells were drilled using a diamond core rig.  Because of problems with running 

sand, drill steel was trapped in many of the boreholes, and resulted in the need to re-drill at 

many of the locations.  To avoid problems with the drill rods getting stuck in the boreholes, 

some wells utilized a combination of core and mud rotary to allow safer drilling to greater 

depths.  Ultimately, it was decided to drill well PGMW17-11 only with mud rotary to avoid 

excessive delays in the drilling program that had been experienced with the core drilling. 

 

10.2.2  Brine Pumping Well PGPW16-01  
 

To date, one new exploration pumping test well, PGPW16-01, has been drilled, 

constructed, and tested. A schematic diagram for well PGPW16-01 is shown on Figure A-8 

(Appendix A).  The drilling contractor was Hidrotec based in Salta, Argentina.  Location and 

sample information for the exploration well are given in Table 10.7.  
 

Table 10.7.  Location and Depth for Pumping Well PGPW16-01  
 

Exploration Well Identifier 
Total Depth 

(meters) 
UTM Easting1  

(meters, POSGAR 94) 
UTM Northing1  

(meters, POSGAR 94) 

PGPW16-01 351 3,429,204 7,283,655 
1 UTM Easting and Northing from a hand-held portable GPS. 
 

The following represents a brief summary of the equipment and methods utilized during 

construction of the well. 

 

• Drilled using conventional circulation mud rotary.  Drilling fluid was polymer mixed 
with brine.  

• Drilled borehole diameter was 17-inch from land surface to 125 meters, and 131/2-inch 
to total depth. 

• For each exploration well, time to drill 2 meters was recorded to monitor penetration 
rate. 

• Unwashed and washed drill cuttings were described and stored in labeled plastic cutting 
boxes. 

• Once drilling was completed, 10-inch blank PVC casing, and 6-inch slotted PVC well 
screen was installed (slot size 0.75 mm).  

• Gravel pack (1-3 mm diameter) was installed in the annular space surrounding the well 
screen.  

 



78 

 

After installation of casing, gravel pack, and fill materials, polymer mud was broken 

down using sodium hypochlorite solution.  The well was developed using compressed air.  The 

sand content of produced brine was monitored during development using an Imhoff cone.  

Upon completion of development, the well flowed naturally for more than 2 months until the 

annular space could be cement-sealed.  Following sealing the annular space, the casing at land 

surface was fully isolated. 

 
The pumping test at well PGPW16-01 started on May 17, 2017 with an average flow 

rate of 27.7 L/s.  Testing details are given in Table 10.8.  Figure 10.3 shows the discharge 

apparatus used during testing.  Water level was measured in the pumped well with a graduated 

sounder at regular intervals and with a pressure transducer (Solinst levelogger).  Flow rate was 

measured using a flowmeter and with a V-notch weir. The in-line flowmeter measured both 

instantaneous and cumulative flow. Both the flowmeter and the v-notch flow values were 

similar.  During the test, field parameters (pH, T°, Electrical Conductivity (CE) and density) 

were measured, using calibrated CE-meter and pH-meter. Density was measured with a 

hydrometer. pH values ranged from 6.16 to 6.38, CE from 149.5 – 167.7 and density from 

1.196 – 1.203 g/cm3. After approximately 30 hours of testing, the EC-pH meter malfunctioned 

and parameters were not obtained. The pumping test stopped on May 20, 2017 after 57 hours 

because of a failure of the booster pump used to convey the pumped brine away from the 

pumped well, and was terminated when the pump failed again after about 60 hours of pumping.

Semi-logarithmic drawdown and recovery graphs for the pumped well, and nearby 

observation wells PGMW16-01, PGMW16-01b, SW03PG-1 and SW03PG-2, are given on 

Figures C-1 through C-5 (Appendix C), with computed aquifer transmissivity for the interval 

tested. Wells SW03PG-1 and SW03PG-2 were drilled in year 2012 for Eramine, but well 

completion is unknown for both wells.  Observation wells PGMW16-01, PGMW16-01b and 

SW03PG-02 were not analyzed because there was not enough drawdown to obtain a reliable 

value.  

 

Transmissivity is the rate at which water is transmitted through a unit width of aquifer 

under a unit hydraulic gradient and has unit of meters squared per day (m2/d).  For analysis, 

drawdown data were analyzed for aquifer transmissivity using the semi-logarithmic graphical 

method developed by Cooper and Jacob (1946).  Water level recovery measurements were 

analyzed using the Theis (1935) recovery method.  Both methods were analyzed using 

Aqtesolv software (HydroSOLVE, 2008) and verified manually.  Fitted lines and analytical 

results are shown on each graph (Figures C-1 through C-5).  Results are tabulated in 

Table 10.9.

The difference between computed transmissivity from drawdown (1,100 m2/d) and 

recovery (550 m2/d) for the pumped well is believed to be the result of water level recovery 

from previous unchecked flow from the pumped well which overestimates transmissivity 

computed from drawdown measurements, and underestimates transmissivity computed from 

recovery measurements. Based on testing, transmissivity is conservatively estimated to be 550 

m2/d, but may be as large as approximately 1,000 m2/d, and is judged by the author to be 

relatively large for a salar setting. 

 

10.2.3  Downhole Temperature and Electrical Conductivity Surveys 
 

Electrical conductivity is a measure of the water's ability to conduct electricity, and is 

an indirect measure of the water's ionic activity and dissolved solids content.  Because 

electrical conductivity is positively correlated with brine concentration, and brine 

concentration in these salar basins tends to correlate well with lithium concentration, downhole 

surveys can provide an indirect measurement of lithium potential.  In addition, downhole 

electrical conductivity surveys are a good method for identifying freshwater / brine transition 

zones.    

 



81 

 

Following installation of 2-inch PVC in the exploration coreholes, and after waiting for 

the brine inside the casing to equilibrate to the surrounding aquifer, a down-hole electrical 

conductivity profile was conducted at the following five cased coreholes: PGMW16-02, 

PGMW17-04b, PGMW17-05c, PGMW17-07d, and PGMW17-11 (Figures B-3, B-6, B-9, B-

16, and B-21).  Temperature and specific electrical conductivity profiles, as well as laboratory-

measured density and electrical conductivity, are given in Appendix D, Figures D-1 

through D-5. 

 

Electrical conductivity is a measure of the water's ability to conduct electricity, and is 

an indirect measure of the water's ionic activity and dissolved solids content.  Electrical 

conductivity is positively correlated with brine concentration.  The purpose of the profiles was 

to: 

• Determine the electrical conductivity profile and identify potential freshwater 

influence and low density 

• Provide additional verification for the chemistry profiles generated from depth-

specific samples 

 

For each corehole, electrical conductivity and temperature were measured at  
3-meter intervals using an In-Situ brand Aquatroll 100 downhole electrical conductivity probe.  

The probe was calibrated with a standard solution before each survey.  Three 1-minute 

measurements were obtained at each depth station; the average of the three measurements was 

used to generate the profile.  Measurements were taken only while lowering the probe through 

the column of brine.   320 meters was the maximum depth for the profiles because of the 

depth/pressure limitation of the Aquatroll.   

 

Inspection of Figures D-1 through D-5, shows that there is a reasonably good 

correlation between the Aquatroll measurements of specific conductivity, and the laboratory 

measurements of the depth-specific samples.  This supports the reliability of the depth-specific 

samples obtained during the Phase II exploration program.  

 



82 

 

Using the results from the downhole electrical conductivity profiles, it appears that 

there is a fresh water influence in the upper part of well PGMW17-11 (Figure D-5).  However, 

as can be seen on the well completion profile, the upper 279 meters consists of blank casing. 

Therefore, the Aquatroll profile for the upper 279 meters of the blank casing zone is not valid, 

even though a correlation appears to exist between the Aquatroll profile and the laboratory 

results from the depth-specific samples.  The fresh water encountered by the Aquatroll may 

have entered to the inside of the casing during initial casing installation.

11.  SAMPLE PREPARATION, ANALYSES AND SECURITY  
 
 The following section applies only to the Phase II exploration program conducted by 

Millennial Lithium.  The Sample Preparation, Analyses, and Security methods applied during 

the previous Phase I exploration program were documented previously by Montgomery & 

Associates (2017). 

11.1  SAMPLING PROTOCOL 
 

Brine chemistry samples were analyzed by Norlab S.R.L. of Jujuy and by SGS 

Argentina, S.A.. Norlab is in partnership with Alex Stewart Assayers of Mendoza, Argentina, 

who have extensive experience analyzing lithium-bearing brines.  The Alex Stewart and SGS 

Laboratories are accredited to ISO 9001 and operate according to standards consistent with 

ISO 17025 methods at other laboratories.  Selected duplicate samples were obtained by 

Montgomery & Associates and sent to the University of Antofagasta, Chile, as part of the 

QA/QC procedure.   

 

Porosity analyses were conducted by Core Laboratories Petroleum Services Division, 

Houston, Texas.  Core Laboratories provides state of the art petrophysical and geological 

analysis and interpretation of core samples from rock, and has demonstrated that its Quality 

Management System is in compliance with ISO 9000:2008 Certificate of Registration.  

Selected representative samples were submitted for laboratory analyses.  Microsamples of 

brine, obtained from the core samples submitted to Core Laboratories have been requested and 

will be analyzed by ALS Laboratories in Vancouver, Canada, an ISO accredited and well-

established laboratory. Later in the program, samples were analyzed to the same standards for 

porosity by GeoSystems Analysis, Inc of Tucson, Arizona. 

11.2  SAMPLE PREPARATION 
 

Brine samples used to understand the 3-dimensional chemical distribution of lithium in 

the basin included the following sources:  

• depth-specific packer sampling during coring, 
• drive-points during coring, and 



89 

 

• brine samples obtained near the end of the pumping tests in the exploration 
wells. 

 

In addition to brine samples, core samples were also obtained during the program and 

submitted for drainable porosity laboratory testing.  Preliminary analytical results of drainable 

porosity samples are also shown on schematic diagrams of coreholes (Appendix B). 

  

Neither chemistry samples (brine) nor porosity samples (core) were subjected to any 

further preparation prior to shipment to participating laboratories.  After the samples were 

sealed on site, they were processed for the database in the Millennial offices in Salta, then 

shipped in sealed containers to the laboratories for analysis. 

11.2.1  Brine samples from the depth-specific packer sampling  
 

 Most of the brine samples obtained during the 2016 and 2017 drilling program were 

obtained from depth-specific packer sampling during core drilling.  Packer sample were 

obtained during drilling, and sometimes after drilling was completed.  Samples were 

considered acceptable and representative of the interval being sampled when minimal to no 

traces of drilling mud from the corehole were observed in the sample obtained from the packer.  

 
11.2.2  Brine sampling using drive-point samplers 
 

A total of five brine samples were collected using the drive-point sampling technique.  

Brine samples were collecting by removing the core barrel, and installing a drive-point onto 

BT size drill rods.  The drive-point was driven to a depth below the drill bit using a drop 

hammer on the drill rig.  An impermeable diaphragm located just above the drive point 

prevented filling of the BT drill rods during driving.  After driving the drive-point to the desired 

depth, an electric water level sounder was lowered into the BT drill rods to assure the interior 

of the rods were dry.  The sounder was removed, and the diaphragm was perforated using a 

weighted pin lowered with the wireline.  This piercing allowed brine to flow into the drive 

point and begin filling the BT rods.  After bailing and discarding the first fluid, the brine sample 

was bailed from the drill rods.   

 



90 

 

 

11.2.3  Brine samples from the pumping test program 
 

Brine samples were collected directly from the discharge pipe at regular intervals 

during testing. The samples were sent to Alex Stewart and Norlab in sealed 250-milliliter 

plastic bottles with sample numbers clearly identified. Temperature and density were recorded 

on internal field sheets. 

11.2.4  Drainable porosity sampling methodology  
 

 Porosity samples were collected from intact HQ-3 and NQ-3 core. After core retrieval 

using a wireline system, the core was inspected and relatively undisturbed samples were 

selected for porosity analysis. Full diameter core with no visible fractures was selected and 

submitted for laboratory analyses.  The selected sleeved core samples were capped with plastic 

caps, sealed with tape, weighed, and stored for shipment.  Typical length of sample is 15 to 40 

centimeters (cm).  Figure 11.1 is a photo of an example of a core sample prepared for shipping. 

Porosity samples were shipped to Core Laboratories in Houston, Texas, and to Geosystems 

Analysis in Tucson, Arizona for analysis.   

 
 

Figure 11.1: Porosity Sample (HQ-3 Core) Sealed for Shipment 
 

In addition to analyzing intact core samples, samples of loose sediment were also 

analyzed for porosity.  Several sandy zones in the aquifer are very poorly cemented.  It was 



91 

 

decided to send these to Geosystems Analysis for drainable porosity analysis also as they likely 

represent zones of large hydraulic conductivity and drainable porosity and therefore important 

during future brine extraction.  Loose sediment samples were repacked by the lab and then 

tested for drainable porosity.  Repacked samples are identified as such on the well schematics 

in Appendix B. 

 

11.3  BRINE ANALYSIS  

11.3.1  Analytical Methods 
 

Alex Stewart, Norlabs and SGS were the primary laboratory for analysis of brine 

samples. In order to provide a quick response, Alex Stewart employed Inductively Coupled 

Plasma Analysis ("ICP") as the analytical technique for the primary constituents of interest, 

including: boron, calcium, potassium, lithium, magnesium and sulphur. Samples were diluted 

100:1 before analysis. 

Sulphate was assayed using the turbidimetric method, with check assaying 20% of the 

samples using the gravimetric method. Subsequent samples were analyzed using only the 

gravimetric method. The argentometric method was used for assaying chloride and volumetric 

analysis (acid/base titration) was used for carbonates (alkalinity as CaCO3). Laboratory 

measurements were conducted for Total Dissolved Solids (TDS), density, and pH.  

11.3.2  Analytical Quality Assurance and Quality Control (QA/QC) 
 

The QA/QC) documented herein addresses brine samples collected during drilling and 

during pumping. Part of the duplicate samples were used for QA/QC procedures, and the 

remaining duplicate samples properly stored for future reference. 

 

The quality control program included random insertion of field blanks, duplicates, and 

a standard. About 20 percent of the samples sent for laboratory analyses were quality control 

samples.  The data was compiled by Millennial staff for confirmation of the accuracy and 

precision of the analysis, and reviewed by Montgomery & Associates. 

 



92 

 

11.3.3  Field Blanks 
 

 To date, a total of eight blank samples have been submitted to the laboratories for 

chemical analyses.  The blank samples consisted of distilled water.  A total of 13 samples were 

submitted to Norlab (Alex Stewart); seven were submitted to SGS.  Neither lab detected any 

lithium.  Most components were not detected, and for those constituents detected, extremely 

small quantities were reported. 

 

11.3.4  Standard Sampling 
 

Two types of standards were used in the 2106/2017 Phase II sampling program.  The 

first standard consisted of a large sample of the Pastos Grandes salar brine was collected during 

testing at well PGPW16-01 to function as a "standard" that is regularly submitted to the 

laboratories.  This sample was used regularly as part of a round robin style quality control 

check.  This standard sample also functioned as a type of duplicate sample to monitor possible 

changes in the ability of the laboratories to replicate the results of the standard sample during 

the course of the sampling program at selected laboratories. Laboratory results of the 

"standard" sample are given in Table 11.1.  

 

Table 11.1.  Laboratory Chemical Analysis for the PGPW16-01 Standard 

 
 

The second type of standard consisted of a synthetic standard that was commissioned

11.3.7  QA/QC Conclusions and Recommendations 
 

The field sampling of brines from the pumping tests was done in accordance with 

generally accepted industry standards. The quality control data based upon the insertion of 

standards, field blanks and field duplicates indicate that the analytical data are accurate, and 

the samples being analyzed are representative of the brine within the aquifer.  As a result, the 

authors are confident that the reported results are representative of the brine chemistry in the 

salar.  Although the analyses of Norlab/Alex Stewart and SGS laboratories show some 

inconsistencies, in general they show statistically acceptable accuracy for Li, K and Mg 

analyses.  For future phases of exploration, QAQC procedures will be implemented and 

additional laboratories possibly investigated.

11.4  DRAINABLE POROSITY ANALYSIS 
 

11.4.1  Laboratory Analytical Procedures for Drainable Porosity 
 

Laboratory analytical procedure for drainable porosity by centrifuge as described by 

Core Laboratories consisted of the following steps: 

1. Cut 38 mm (1.5-inch) diameter cylindrical plug from sample material (plunge cut or 
drill); typical length is about 45 mm (1.75-inch) 

2. Freeze sample material with dry ice if needed to maintain integrity 
3. Caliper bulk volume of the cylindrical plug, and weigh sample 
4. Encapsulate plug as needed in Teflon and nickel foil, with nickel screen on ends of 

plugs, and weigh encapsulated sample 
5. Calculate bulk density as (Mass of plug before encapsulation)/(Caliper bulk volume) 
6. Place plug in brine and saturate under vacuum to ensure full saturation:  Corelab uses 

a standard sodium chloride brine containing 244,000 ppm NaCl.  The standard brine 
has a density of 1.184 gm/cm3.   Core Laboratories will saturate samples using brine 
provided by Millennial, if needed. 

7. Record weight of saturated core 
8. Desaturate samples in high speed centrifuge for 4 hours.  Spin rates were calculated to 

give drainage pressure of 1 pound per square inch (psi) for poorly cemented or loose 
sands; and 5 psi for clay and halite.  Pressure was calculated at the center of the plug 
placed in the centrifuge. The sample is then centrifuged at .5 psi for 4 hours. 

9. Collect any drainage and record volume; effluent is saved for possible analysis at ALS 
Environmental in Vancouver). Fluid collected from these cores are not representative 
of in situ brines if re-saturation with NaCl is needed. 

10. Remove plug from centrifuge and record weight.   
a. Drained fluid volume is calculated as (saturated plug weight – drained plug 

weight)/1.184 
b. Drainable porosity is calculated as (Drained fluid volume)/(Caliper bulk 

volume)  
 

Drainable porosity is given as a fraction of the total rock volume and is unitless.  For 

example, if a rock has a volume of 100 milliliter (ml), and 10 ml of fluid can drain from the 

rock, the drainable porosity is 10/100, or 0.10.  Although determined by laboratory methods, 

the drainable porosity is essentially the same as specific yield as defined in classical aquifer 

mechanics.   

 
 
 



102 

 

11.4.2  Laboratory Analytical Procedures for Total Porosity 
 

After drainable porosity measurements, the plug samples from the centrifuge were 

analyzed for total porosity, using the following steps: 

1. Oven dry sample for 5 days at 115.6 degrees Celsius (240 degrees Fahrenheit) 
2. Weigh oven-dried sample 
3. Assume that all weight loss is pure water lost from pore space:  Therefore volume of 

water lost due to oven-drying is calculated as  
((Drained plug weight)-(Oven-dried plug weight))/(water density of 1 gm/cc) 

4. Total porosity is calculated as ((Drained fluid volume)+(Oven drying fluid 
loss))/(Caliper bulk volume) 

 

Total porosity, like drainable porosity, is given as a fraction of the total rock volume and is 

unitless.  Because total porosity is not representative of the extractable brine resource, total 

porosity values will not be used to estimate the Resource.   

 

11.4.3  Laboratory Analytical Procedures for Repacked Sediment Samples 
 

All loose sediment samples were analyzed by Geosystems Analysis laboratory in 

Tucson, Arizona.  The following description was provided by the laboratory. 

 

11.4.3.1 Preparation 
All loose and sandy samples were packed with moderate effort into test cells without 

knowledge of prior bulk density or other consolidation tests. Extra repacking was performed 

on samples with minimum effort and maximum effort to test the effectiveness and variation of 

hand-packing at higher and lower densities. Approximately 0.1 gram per cubic centimeter 

(g/cm3) lower and higher bulk densities were achieved, respectively. 

11.4.3.2 Packing the Core 
Sandy material was packed in several small lifts into a stainless-steel ring. The weight 

and packing height from the first lift was used to guide the rest of the lifts for consistent density 

packing. Equipment, cell, and sample weights were tracked by scales throughout the process. 

A final packed and assembled core weight was recorded. 



103 

 

11.4.3.3 Saturating the Core 
A template was used to calculate the amount of brine solution needed to saturate the 

soil. Plastic air tubing (approximately 6" length) was inserted into the top of each core to 

monitor saturation and prevent brine solution spillage.  Assembled cores were saturated slowly 

from the bottom up using the supplied brine solution and a combination of gravity feed and 

vacuum suction (if target saturation could not be met using gravity feed) for upwards of 24 

hours. Fully saturated cores were closed at the bottom with a hose clamp to prevent brine 

solution loss and disconnected from the saturation setup. 

11.4.3.4 Brine Release Testing 
Each cell assembly was transferred to a test rack for three pressure steps.  The first 0 

mbar pressure step was applied for 24 hours to remove oversaturation solution.  Two sequential 

pressure steps, 120 millibar and 1/3 bar (estimated field water capacity, MOSA, 2002 Part 4 

Ch. 3, 3.3.3.2), were used to approximate brine solution release at 120 mbar and 1/3 bar of the 

brine solution.  The 120 millibar pressure step was maintained for 2 days and the 1/3 bar was 

continued for another 2 to 4 days.  Weight measurements were performed twice a day to 

determine loss of brine solution over time.  Cores were disassembled and samples were oven 

dried after the final step to determine total porosity (MOSA, 2002, Part 4 Ch. 2, 2.3.2.1).  

Brine solution release volumes at the 120 millibar and at 1/3 bar pressure steps were 

estimated as the difference between the measured total porosity and moisture retained after the 

pressure plate measurements (MOSA, 2002, Part 4 Ch3, 3.3.3.5).  The solution release volume 

(drainable porosity) at 1/3 bar was considered to approximate the maximum solution drainage 

under gravity/pumping conditions and therefore specific yield.   

11.4.3.5 Data Entry and Data Analysis 
Estimated particle density and weight data from core samples at different pressure steps 

over time were entered into the spreadsheet. Salt weight left in the sample after drying, 

estimated porosity and water content change were automatically calculated in the spreadsheet.  

Particle density was optimized during data processing by using all prior test measurements, 

and a solver in Microsoft Excel.  The calculated particle density for each sample was presented 

in the laboratory report. 



104 

 

 

11.5  SAMPLE SECURITY 
 

All samples were labeled with permanent marker, sealed with tape and stored at a 

secure site, both in the field, and in Salta, Argentina, until transported to the laboratory for 

analysis. Samples were packed into secured boxes with chain of custody forms and then 

shipped to the appropriate laboratories in Argentina and the United States.  



105 

 

12.  DATA VERIFICATION  
 
 

Michael Rosko (independent QP) conducted with assistance of lawyer Rafael 

Arganaraz, the following forms of data verification: 

▪ Visits to the Project site, approving drill hole locations, and review of 
infrastructure in the field and at the camp in Santa Rosa de los Pastos Grandes. 
▪ Inspection of original laboratory results for the Eramine and Millennial brine 
datasets; 
▪ Review of publicly available information from adjacent properties in Salar de 
Pastos Grandes. 

 

Michael Rosko and Montgomery & Associates employees have been to site to verify 

field operations, have reviewed core and cuttings descriptions in the field, were on-site during 

aquifer testing at well PGPW16-01, obtained independent brine samples for analysis by the 

University of Antofagasta in Chile, and have checked summary chemistry tables against 

original laboratory reports. 

 

12.1  Data Management During Millennial Field Program  
 

During the Phase II exploration program, a large amount of information was being 

obtained and managed.  It was critical for the project that data were readily accessible, properly 

archived, and backed up.  The information to be compiled during the program includes: 

 

• Field notes:  The field geologists and hydrogeologists record field notes concurrently 
with the recorded observation; not at a later date.  Observations include date, time, 
name initials, well name, UTM coordinates, activities, observations, etc.  These notes 
are entered directly into the field computer on site.  

• Physical parameters: At the time of sampling, field physical parameters are measured 
and recorded for all fluid samples.  These parameters include temperature, pH, density, 
and electrical conductivity.  The field geologist notes and records the sample color, 
odor, presence of hydrocarbon sheen, and presence of gas, and suspended solids. 

• Lithological description: Drill core and drill cuttings are described by Millennial 
geologists using standard forms and checked by a Montgomery & Associates 
hydrogeologist. These forms are in paper and will be completed by the crew.  

• Sample description and Chain of Custody (COC):  During field operations, sediment 
samples are collected for porosity analyses, and brine solution collected for chemical 
analyses.  A standard COC is prepared for all samples submitted to laboratories. 



106 

 

• Project Database: Lithologic data are entered into the project database designed and 
maintained by Millennial.  All sample data for both porosity and brine samples are 
entered into the same database.  

• Summary tables: Details of porosity and brine sampling, and well construction are 
prepared by Millennial geologists in the field and reviewed by Montgomery & 
Associates hydrogeologists. These tables include UTM coordinates, elevation, total 
depth, casing installation and perforated section, and water level. Similar tables are 
prepared by Millennial personnel in Salta and document receipt of samples from the 
field, dates for sending samples to laboratories, and laboratory results.   

• Daily drill reports:  These are prepared by the current drilling contractor Hidrotec and 
describe all payment items, mechanical issues, machine maintenance, crew names, and 
site conditions. 

• Daily activity logs: Millennial geologist in the field prepare and summarize the field 
activities at each work site on a daily basis.  It is kept in the main computer and backup 
in an external hard drive.  Daily activity logs are sent to Project personnel and 
consultants as needed. 
 

  



107 

 

13.  MINERAL PROCESSING AND METALLURGICAL TESTING 
 

No metallurgical testing or assessment of potential mineral processing regimes has been 

conducted to date.  

 
  



108 

 

14.  MINERAL RESOURCE ESTIMATES FOR LITHIUM AND POTASSIUM: 
MEASURED, INDICATED, AND INFERRED RESOURCES 

 
 

This initial Phase II resource calculation consists of Measured, Indicated, and Inferred 

resource estimates.  The key parameters of brine mineral grade and drainable porosity are used 

to compute the Measured, Indicated, and Inferred resource for the Pastos Grandes project.  The 

industry-acceptable method of constructing polygonal blocks surrounding coreholes, and 

dividing the polygons into horizontal layers by hydrogeologic units is used.  The resource 

model includes only discrete-depth values for brine chemistry, and drainable porosity 

determined from core analyses, as well as the use of representative values for where depth-

specific samples did not exist or were not representative due to field or lab problems. Results 

from pumping and packer tests, and downhole electrical conductivity profiles supported the 

values used, but were not used directly in the resource calculations. 

 

14.1  DEFINITION OF POLYGONS BLOCKS 
  

 Total area of polygonal blocks used in the resource calculations is 23.2 km2, as shown 

on Figure 14.1.  Claims that are not owned or optioned by Millennial were excluded from 

resource calculations.   

 



109 

 

 
Figure 14.1.  Polygons Used for Resource Calculations  

 

With the exception of the alluvial fans to the north, most polygon blocks are completely 

within the basin floor of Pastos Grandes basin, as defined by photo interpretation of satellite 

images. Each polygon block contains at least one, relatively deep diamond drill hole, except 



110 

 

for PGMW17-11, which was drilled only by mud rotary methods.  Boundaries between 

polygon blocks are generally equidistant from diamond drill holes.  For most polygon blocks, 

outer boundaries are the same as basin boundaries, as discussed above.  However, in the case 

of the polygon on the west side of the basin containing PGMW17-07d, because the overall 

thickness of the polygon used to estimate the resource was 510 meters, we excluded 200 meters 

adjacent to the Tertiary basin boundary to account for probable shallower sediment thicknesses 

adjacent to the basin boundary.   

 

For polygon blocks containing boreholes PGMW17-04b and PGMW17-06c, the 

southern boundary of the polygon block was an extended boundary where the authors' 

conceptualization of hydrogeologic conditions suggests a strong likelihood that brine exists at 

depth.   In addition, the results of VES geophysical survey results and demonstrated depth-

specific brine samples at PGMW17-11 were used to infer brine at depth to the north and extend 

the polygons.  In both cases, the extensions based on conceptualization and/or geophysical 

surveys were categorized only as Inferred. 

 

 

14.2  DEFINITION OF HYDROGEOLOGIC UNITS 
 

Results of Phase I and Phase II exploration drilling indicate that basin-fill deposits in 

Pastos Grandes can be subdivided into hydrogeologic units that are dominated by five 

lithologies, as was previously describe in Section 8.3 (Table 8.1).  Predominant lithology, and 

number of analyses for drainable porosity of these units are given in Table 14.1. 

 

  



111 

 

Table 14.1.  Summary of Drainable Porosity Values

Gravel and breccia 0 --- 3 0.13 0 --- 

 
 

Most of the drainable porosity values provided by Core Laboratories are not believed 

to be reliable.  Comparison of the sediments encountered in Pastos Grandes with other nearby 

basins show that the hydrogeologic units in Pastos Grandes are typical of salar basins in the 

region.  However, the drainable porosity results from Core Laboratories are substantially lower 

than other projects in the region, and also extremely low compared to results from Geosystems 

Analysis for similar hydrogeologic units.  Upon review, several errors by the laboratory 

resulted in excessive delays in processing.  These delays resulted in core being allowed to 

partially dry out, and caused crystallization of the salts in the brine in the pore spaces.  This 

crystallization is believed to have reduced drainable porosity measurements in the clastic 

samples.   

 

In addition, many of the halite samples that were measured by Core Laboratories were 

massive in nature (solid halite), and not representative of the mixed nature of the unit.  For 

example, well PGMW17-05 (Figure B-7) shows a number of halite samples with effectively 

zero drainable porosity measurements.  But depth-specific packer sampling over a 2-meter 

interval was able to extract brine from the unit, demonstrating the permeable nature of clastic 

interbeds in the mixed halite unit.    



112 

 

 

As a result of the processing issues, Millennial changed laboratories for the latter half 

of the Phase II exploration program and sent core and repacked sediment samples to 

Geosystems Analysis.  As can be seen on Table 14.1, the drainable porosity values provided 

by Geosystems Analysis are larger, and more similar to values reported by other projects in 

the region.  The results for the repacked sediment samples were considered only subjectively 

because repacked loose material tends to have overestimated drainable porosity results as 

compared to in-situ, undisturbed samples.  However, the results demonstrate that within the 

very fine-grained and evaporate units, loose sandy units exist and therefore support the 

drainable porosity values described in the next section used to determine the resource.  

14.3  TOTAL RESOURCE ESTIMATION 
 

Each borehole was divided into hydrogeologic units using the five predominant 

lithologies given above.  Drainable porosity values for each hydrogeologic unit within a single 

polygon were computed by averaging the available drainable porosity data from within the 

hydrogeologic unit at the polygon borehole.  There were a few polygons in which some 

hydrogeologic units contained no porosity data.  For these units, drainable porosity was 

estimated similar lithologies from the Sal de Vida Project, or assigned based on similar 

lithologies in other Hombre Muerto boreholes, or conservative drainable porosity values were 

estimated from values reported in the literature (Johnson, 1967) and assigned based on 

lithology, as follows in Table 14.2. 

 

Table 14.2.  Assigned Drainable Porosity Values 

PREDOMINANT LITHOLOGY OF 
HYDROGEOLOGIC UNIT 

ASSIGNED DRAINABLE 
POROSITY 

  

Clay and silt 0.02 

Mixed halite 0.03 

Mixed sand and silt 0.14 

Sandstone 0.16 

Gravel and breccia 0.16 



113 

 

 
 

The porosity of the resource volume varies with geology but to date effective porosity 

has been predictable within distinct hydrostratigraphic units; the weighted average for the 

entire saturated aquifer considered in the resource is approximately 9.5%, and is considered 

reasonable by the author based on experience in salar basins with a large percentage of clastic 

sediments. 

 

For those instances in which a hydrogeologic unit within an individual borehole had no 

depth-specific brine sample, the analyses from the nearest sample, or samples, either above 

and/or below the unit, were averaged and that value applied to the entire unit.  However, 

because the lithium concentration at any given drilling location was extremely uniform 

regardless of the depth, the method is believed to be valid in all cases where it was applied. 

 

Drainable porosity and lithium content are weighted by hydrogeologic unit thickness. 

Saturated thickness for the uppermost hydrogeologic units is estimated from the depth to water 

in the polygon's central well to the base of the hydrogeologic unit.  Thickness of the lowermost 

hydrogeologic unit is limited by total depth of the core hole.  It is assumed that the properties 

at the borehole for hydrogeologic unit thickness, drainable porosity, lithium, and potassium 

extend continuously throughout the entire polygon.  The resource computed for each polygon 

is independent of adjacent polygons.  The computed resource for each polygon was the sum of 

the products of saturated hydrogeologic unit thickness, polygon area, drainable porosity, and 

lithium and potassium content.  Table 14.3 summarizes the resource calculated for each 

individual polygon (Figure 14.1).  Table 14.4 summarizes the lithium resource by unit for 

each polygon.  Table 14.5 summarizes the potassium resource by unit for each polygon.

were excluded by the cutoff grade were for the Indicated and Inferred polygons at the north 

area where fresh water was encountered in the upper 200 meters (Figures 14.1 and B-21 in 

Appendix B) and lithium concentrations were less than 300 mg/L.

The reader is cautioned that mineral resources are not mineral reserves and do not have demonstrated 
economic viability. 
 

The total contained lithium and potassium values are based on measurements of 

effective (drainable) porosity distributed throughout the aquifer volume that defines this 

resource. This method of porosity determination is designed to estimate the portion of the total 

porosity that can theoretically be drained by pumping; however, these in-situ estimates may 

differ from total extractable quantities.  

 
14.3.1  Dominant Hydrogeologic Units 
 

 The dominant hydrogeologic unit encountered during drilling for the Pastos Grandes 

Project has been mixed sand and silt, followed by mixed halite.  Mixed sand and silt also 

dominates the total amount of brine used to estimate the resource.  However, because the 

sandstone unit is considerably more permeable than the mixed halite unit, the sandstone 



117 

 

contributes more to the total drainable brine in the system, even though volumetrically, halite 

is more dominant. These relations are shown in the Table 14.7. 

 

Table 14.7.  Percent of Brine Volume by Hydrogeologic Unit

14.3.2  Resource Average Grade 
 

 Estimated drainable volume of brine within the polygons having lithium concentration 

exceeding 300 mg/L, is 1.25 x 109 cubic meters.  Therefore, average lithium grade for the 

Measured and Indicated resource is approximately 445 mg/L as lithium.  Average Measured 

and Indicated potassium grade calculated in the same way is about 4,747 mg/L as potassium.  

Because the resource is a brine, grades are expected to change during production pumping.  

The 163 brine samples analyzed during the drilling program yielded an average 

magnesium:lithium (Mg/Li) ratio of 6.3, and average sulphate:lithium (SO4/Li) ratio of 18.2. 

 

14.3.3  Confidence Level of Resource Estimate  
The authors' conceptual understanding of the hydrogeologic nature of the Pastos 

Grandes Salar is strong in the concession areas controlled by Millennial.  Observed results are 

consistent with anticipated stratigraphic and hydrogeologic conditions associated with mature, 

closed-basin, high altitude salar systems having freshwater recharge from a perennial river.  

One of the most important features is the general consistency of the lithium and potassium 

grades measured throughout the entire area.  Although brackish water zones exist near 



118 

 

freshwater recharge areas to the north, and result in lower grades due to fresh water mixing 

with brine, these zones were anticipated and have been removed from the resource estimate.  

Aside from these areas, the majority of the salar contains a high-density brine with an average 

lithium grade over 450 mg/L, with a substantial amount of this brine contained in permeable 

sands and sandstones. 

 

Based on the author's current understanding of the hydrogeologic system of Pastos 

Grandes, the relative consistency of the data, and confidence in the drilling and sampling 

results achieved to date, the author has sufficient grounds to report Measured and Indicated 

resources along with additional Inferred resources for the Project.  Using a guideline reported 

by Houston et al. (2011), where in a mature salar system, a well spacing of 3-4 kilometers is 

recommended to allow categorization of the brine as Measured; a minimum spacing of 2.5 

kilometers is recommended for immature salars for a Measured categorization.  Approximate 

average well spacing for the recently-drilled Millennial exploration wells is about 2 kilometers 

(Figure 14.1). 

 

14.3.4  Conversion of Li and K to Equivalents  
 It is common in the lithium and potassium industries to report lithium and potassium 

metals as equivalents.  Lithium carbonate (Li2CO3) is a commonly reported equivalent for 

lithium; potassium chloride (KCl) is a commonly reported equivalent for potassium.  The 

conversion factors used to calculate the equivalents from their metal ions is simple and based 

on the molar weight for the elements added to generate the equivalent.  The equations are as 

follows: 

 

Li x 5.3228 = lithium carbonate equivalent 

K x 1.907 = potassium chloride equivalent  

 

Results of the breakdown for lithium and potassium equivalents resources in each category are 

summarized in Table 14.8.

25.  INTERPRETATION AND CONCLUSIONS 
 

Based on the results of the Phase I and Phase II exploration programs, the author 

concludes that the Pastos Grande Salar Project is a project of merit that justifies continued 

development to evaluate the feasibility of the production of lithium and potassium, and include 

the following interpretations and conclusions. 

 

• Past work by DGFM, Phase I work by Eramine, and Phase II work by Millennial 

confirm elevated and potentially economic lithium-potassium grade brines in the salar.   

• Phase II exploration drilling by Millennial has confirmed that clastic sediments exist to 

depths of at least 601 meters at the Property, and confirm previous geophysical 

interpretations. 

• Depth-specific sampling and review of drill core of the deeper clastic units below the 

mixed halite zone supports the occurrence of a deep, lithium-bearing brine aquifer.  

• Evaluation of the depth-specific brine samples suggests that the brine is relatively 

uniform both horizontally and vertically in the concessions that are located within the 

salar. 

• Exploration drilling in the alluvial fan north of the salar indicates that dense, lithium-

rich brine has migrated north of the salar.  Fresh water occurs in the upper aquifer 

system to a depth of 200 meters at exploration well PGMW17-11 and overlies dense 

brine. 

• Based on preliminary correlation of the hydrogeologic units in the basin supports the 

conceptualization that the sedimentary units beneath the large "island" outcrops are 

continuous with the adjacent units in the salar areas without the outcrops.  This suggests 

that the recently-acquired concessions to the south may also contain similar 

hydrogeologic units and brine quality. 

•  Pumping test results at well PGMP16-1 suggest that properly-constructed production 

wells should be able to yield relatively large quantities of brine in the future. 

  



127 

 

26.  RECOMMENDATIONS  
 

In support of developing and understanding the potential for the Salar de Pastos 

Grandes, the author recommends continuing and expanding the ongoing Phase III exploration 

program.  The recommended program is designed to obtain information on the ability of the 

aquifer to yield brine to properly-constructed wells, and to obtain new information for the 

recently-acquired REMSA properties in the south part of the Project area.  Information from 

the Phase III drilling and testing program should allow for an increased Resource 

characterization, and provide supporting information for a future Mineral Reserve estimation.     

 

With the information on the geometry of the basin and detailed understanding of the 

hydrogeologic units in the basin, the author recommends that a numerical groundwater flow 

model should be prepared to simulate production pumping from a wellfield as part of a 

Feasibility Study designed to estimate Probable and/or Proven Reserves for the Property. 

 

Because the initial results to date appear favorable, the author also recommends 

investigating a fresh water source for the project.  Several of the concessions controlled by 

Millennial appear to include areas that appear to have fresh surface water, or are at least near 

to areas where fresh water is known to exist.  The fresh water exploration program should 

include drilling and testing of shallow wells in areas not adjacent to salar brine.  

 

General cost estimates for the next phase of the project are summarized in Table 26.1.  

Detailed costs are still being developed.  The proposed activities are designed to be completed 

in years 2018 and 2019.  The goal for the proposed activities will be to: 

 

• Develop a preliminary economic assessment for the project 

• Increase the Mineral Resource via additional geophysical surveys, and exploration 

drilling and testing  

• Develop a numerical groundwater flow model for the basin that will be able to project 

response to long-term production wellfield pumping  



128 

 

• Determine fresh water demand and explore for and identify a sustainable source of 

fresh water  

• Develop engineering studies and works to support development of ponds and a pilot 

processing plant  

• Prepare a definitive feasibility study, incorporating a Mineral Reserve with both 

Probable and Proven categories 

• Detailed and as-built engineering 

• Construction and operations permitting

29.  CERTIFICATE OF QUALIFIED PERSON 
 
Certificate of Qualified Person: Michael J. Rosko 
 
As author and reviewer of the Technical Report, dated January 2, 2018, with an effective 
report date of December 22, 2017, I accept responsibility for the entire Technical Report that 
accompanies this Certificate. 
 
I, Michael J. Rosko, MSc., P.G., do hereby certify that: 
 
• I am a principal hydrogeologist and general manager with Montgomery & Associates, 

Consultores, Ltda., Avenida Vitacura 2771, Of. 404, Las Condes, Santiago de Chile. 
• I graduated with a Bachelor of Science degree in Geology from University of Illinois, 

1983.  
• I graduated with a Master of Science in Geology (Sedimentary Petrology focus) from 

University of Arizona in 1986. 
• I am a registered professional geologist in the states of Arizona (25065), California 

(5236), and Texas (6359). 
• I am a registered member of Society for Mining, Metallurgy, and Exploration 

(#4064687), and a member of the National Ground Water Association and International 
Association of Hydrogeologists. 

• I have practiced hydrogeology for more than 30 years, with much of this time working in 
salar basins in Chile and Argentina similar to the Project area.   

• I have read the definition of "Qualified Person" set out in National Instrument 43-101 
("NI 43-101") and certify that by reason of my education and past relevant work 
experience, I fulfill the requirements to be a "qualified person" for the purposes of NI 43-
101. This Technical Report is based on my personal review of information provided by 
Millennial and others, and results of field activities that were partly monitored by 
Montgomery & Associates.  

• I have previously reviewed Phase I technical work in 2011 and 2012, and have visited the 
Property on December 9 and 10, 2016, May 5 and 6, 2017, and previously in April, 2012 
during Phase I pumping tests.  In addition, a Montgomery & Associates field 
hydrogeologist was on site approximately every 4 to 6 weeks during the Phase II drilling 
and sampling. 

• As of the date of this certificate, to the best of my knowledge, information and belief, the 
Technical Report contains all scientific and technical information that is required to be 
disclosed to make the Technical Report not misleading. 

• I am independent of the issuer applying all of the tests in Section 1.5 of National 
Instrument 43-101. I am independent of the Millennial Lithium Corporation and the 
Vendors of the Pastos Grandes Property.

has been prepared in compliance with that instrument and form.

LABORATORY REPORTS FOR BRINE CHEMISTRY

SOLICITANTE: Cristian Guaymas PREPARACION DE MUESTRA: FECHA INGRESO AL LABORATORIO: 30/11/2016

N° DE ENVIO:

BLANCOS ESTANDARES TIPO DE MUESTRA OTRAS

BL: Blanco de limpieza de cuarzo STD: Standard Pun: puntual Tri: Triplicado BIS: Nuevo informe ID: Identificación

BK M: Blanco de muestra VN: Valor nominal Dup: Duplicado Rep: Repetición LCS: Límite de cuantificacion superior COD: Código

BK R: Blanco de reactivo SD: Desviación standard Dup C: Duplicado de cuarteo Com: Compuesta LC: Límite de cuantificación LD: Límite de Detección

Muestreo •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace responsable por cualquier aspecto vinculado a las muestras antes de su entrega al laboratorio, en caso de que Alex Stewart  no sea el extractor de las mismas.

•  Los resultados de los análisis de las muestras extraídas por el cliente, pertenecen solo a las muestras en el estado de las mismas al momento de su ingreso a Alex Stewart Argentina  y a partir de la fecha de recepción de las instrucciones.

Almacenaje •  Los rechazos de muestras sólidas recibidas en ASA Argentina serán almacenadas sin costo durante 3 meses. Para muestras líquidas de salmueras al cabo de 45 días de reportadas las muestras se devolverán al cliente a costo de este.

•  Para muestras sólidas, a partir de esa fecha se cobrará el  almacenaje (precios de P-40), salvo que se reciban instrucciones contrarias. 

•  El cliente puede retirar las muestras de nuestras instalaciones o solicitar su eliminación según procedimientos ambientales aceptados a costo al cliente, siendo él responsable absoluto de la disposición final de las muestras devueltas.

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se responsabiliza por alteraciones o daños que naturalmente puedan ocurrirle a las muestras. Las muestras devueltas al clientes carecen de la adición de cualquier substancia o material que atente al medio ambiente.

Informe •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace cargo por el uso que se de a los resultados obtenidos de nuestros servicios.  

•  El Cliente puede publicar los informes solo en forma completa y aclarando quien es el emisor de los mismos. Para su reproducción parcial deberá solicitar autorizacion a Alex Stewart Argentina 

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  podrá usar para fines estadísticos los resultados de los informes de análisis.

•  Escapa a la responsabilidad de Alex Stewart Argentina la evaluación que pueda surgir sobre la aplicación de los resultados emitidos en nuestros Informes de Ensayos.

•  Los informes preliminares previamente emitidos bajo este mismo número de informe quedan reemplazados por el presente informe analítico final.

QA / QC •  Aspectos concernientes a las validaciones metodológicas, sesgo, precisión e incertidumbres asociadas, pueden ser solicitados por el cliente a Alex Stewart Argentina. 

•  Los Límites de cuantificación informados corresponden a los obtenidos en los procesos de validación del método, pueden variar según la matriz y concentración de la muestra.

•  Las Curvas de Calibración empleadas en las metodologías de análisis tienen coeficientes R
2
 superiores a 0.99.

•  Se procede a informar solamente los resultados que estén enmarcados dentro del rango de validación o entre el LD y el LCS y a los destinatarios que él explícitamente autorice.                                                                                                                                                •  Para Au4-30 el 

Límite de Cuantificación es: LC = 0.06 mg/kg                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              •  Los 

valores informados por debajo del LC tienen estadísticamente un grado de confiabilidad menor.

•  Para  lecturas de Cr, Cu, Fe, Mn, Mo y Ni por ICP: Los límites de detección declarados son solo instrumentales, no involucran el tratamiento de la muestra.

REANALISIS:

CLIENTE: PROYECTOS PASTOS GRANDES S.A. Nº DE COTIZACION: QE-472-2 FECHA RECEPCION DE MUESTRAS: 02/12/2016

DIRECCION: Rep. De Israel 131. salta TOTAL DE MUESTRAS: 6 FECHA RECEPCION DE INSTRUCCIONES: 05/12/2016

SOLICITANTE: Cristian Guaymas PREPARACION DE MUESTRA: FECHA INGRESO AL LABORATORIO: 05/12/2016

PROYECTO: Pastos Grandes FECHA EMISION DE INFORME: 22/12/2016

N° DE ENVIO:

BLANCOS ESTANDARES TIPO DE MUESTRA OTRAS

BL: Blanco de limpieza de cuarzo STD: Standard Pun: puntual Tri: Triplicado BIS: Nuevo informe ID: Identificación

BK M: Blanco de muestra VN: Valor nominal Dup: Duplicado Rep: Repetición LCS: Límite de cuantificacion superior COD: Código

BK R: Blanco de reactivo SD: Desviación standard Dup C: Duplicado de cuarteo Com: Compuesta LC: Límite de cuantificación LD: Límite de Detección

Muestreo •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace responsable por cualquier aspecto vinculado a las muestras antes de su entrega al laboratorio, en caso de que Alex Stewart  no sea el extractor de las mismas.

•  Los resultados de los análisis de las muestras extraídas por el cliente, pertenecen solo a las muestras en el estado de las mismas al momento de su ingreso a Alex Stewart Argentina  y a partir de la fecha de recepción de las instrucciones.

Almacenaje •  Los rechazos de muestras sólidas recibidas en ASA Argentina serán almacenadas sin costo durante 3 meses. Para muestras líquidas de salmueras al cabo de 45 días de reportadas las muestras se devolverán al cliente a costo de este.

•  Para muestras sólidas, a partir de esa fecha se cobrará el  almacenaje (precios de P-40), salvo que se reciban instrucciones contrarias. 

•  El cliente puede retirar las muestras de nuestras instalaciones o solicitar su eliminación según procedimientos ambientales aceptados a costo al cliente, siendo él responsable absoluto de la disposición final de las muestras devueltas.

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se responsabiliza por alteraciones o daños que naturalmente puedan ocurrirle a las muestras. Las muestras devueltas al clientes carecen de la adición de cualquier substancia o material que atente al medio ambiente.

Informe •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace cargo por el uso que se de a los resultados obtenidos de nuestros servicios.  

•  El Cliente puede publicar los informes solo en forma completa y aclarando quien es el emisor de los mismos. Para su reproducción parcial deberá solicitar autorizacion a Alex Stewart Argentina 

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  podrá usar para fines estadísticos los resultados de los informes de análisis.

•  Escapa a la responsabilidad de Alex Stewart Argentina la evaluación que pueda surgir sobre la aplicación de los resultados emitidos en nuestros Informes de Ensayos.

•  Los informes preliminares previamente emitidos bajo este mismo número de informe quedan reemplazados por el presente informe analítico final.

QA / QC •  Aspectos concernientes a las validaciones metodológicas, sesgo, precisión e incertidumbres asociadas, pueden ser solicitados por el cliente a Alex Stewart Argentina. 

•  Los Límites de cuantificación informados corresponden a los obtenidos en los procesos de validación del método, pueden variar según la matriz y concentración de la muestra.

•  Las Curvas de Calibración empleadas en las metodologías de análisis tienen coeficientes R
2
 superiores a 0.99.

•  Se procede a informar solamente los resultados que estén enmarcados dentro del rango de validación o entre el LD y el LCS y a los destinatarios que él explícitamente autorice.                                                                                                                                                •  Para Au4-30 el 

Límite de Cuantificación es: LC = 0.06 mg/kg                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              •  Los 

valores informados por debajo del LC tienen estadísticamente un grado de confiabilidad menor.

•  Para  lecturas de Cr, Cu, Fe, Mn, Mo y Ni por ICP: Los límites de detección declarados son solo instrumentales, no involucran el tratamiento de la muestra.

Muestreo •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace responsable por cualquier aspecto vinculado a las muestras antes de su entrega al laboratorio, en caso de que Alex Stewart  no sea el extractor de las mismas.

•  Los resultados de los análisis de las muestras extraídas por el cliente, pertenecen solo a las muestras en el estado de las mismas al momento de su ingreso a Alex Stewart Argentina  y a partir de la fecha de recepción de las instrucciones.

Almacenaje •  Los rechazos de muestras sólidas recibidas en ASA Argentina serán almacenadas sin costo durante 3 meses. Para muestras líquidas de salmueras al cabo de 45 días de reportadas las muestras se devolverán al cliente a costo de este.

•  Para muestras sólidas, a partir de esa fecha se cobrará el  almacenaje (precios de P-40), salvo que se reciban instrucciones contrarias. 

•  El cliente puede retirar las muestras de nuestras instalaciones o solicitar su eliminación según procedimientos ambientales aceptados a costo al cliente, siendo él responsable absoluto de la disposición final de las muestras devueltas.

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se responsabiliza por alteraciones o daños que naturalmente puedan ocurrirle a las muestras. Las muestras devueltas al clientes carecen de la adición de cualquier substancia o material que atente al medio ambiente.

Informe •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace cargo por el uso que se de a los resultados obtenidos de nuestros servicios.  

•  El Cliente puede publicar los informes solo en forma completa y aclarando quien es el emisor de los mismos. Para su reproducción parcial deberá solicitar autorizacion a Alex Stewart Argentina 

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  podrá usar para fines estadísticos los resultados de los informes de análisis.

•  Escapa a la responsabilidad de Alex Stewart Argentina la evaluación que pueda surgir sobre la aplicación de los resultados emitidos en nuestros Informes de Ensayos.

•  Los informes preliminares previamente emitidos bajo este mismo número de informe quedan reemplazados por el presente informe analítico final.

QA / QC •  Aspectos concernientes a las validaciones metodológicas, sesgo, precisión e incertidumbres asociadas, pueden ser solicitados por el cliente a Alex Stewart Argentina. 

•  Los Límites de cuantificación informados corresponden a los obtenidos en los procesos de validación del método, pueden variar según la matriz y concentración de la muestra.

•  Las Curvas de Calibración empleadas en las metodologías de análisis tienen coeficientes R
2
 superiores a 0.99.

Almacenaje •  Los rechazos de muestras sólidas recibidas en ASA Argentina serán almacenadas sin costo durante 3 meses. Para muestras líquidas de salmueras al cabo de 45 días de reportadas las muestras se devolverán al cliente a costo de este.
•  Para muestras sólidas, a partir de esa fecha se cobrará el  almacenaje (precios de P-40), salvo que se reciban instrucciones contrarias. 

•  El cliente puede retirar las muestras de nuestras instalaciones o solicitar su eliminación según procedimientos ambientales aceptados a costo al cliente, siendo él responsable absoluto de la disposición final de las muestras devueltas.

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se responsabiliza por alteraciones o daños que naturalmente puedan ocurrirle a las muestras. Las muestras devueltas al clientes carecen de la adición de cualquier substancia o material que atente al medio ambiente.

Informe •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace cargo por el uso que se de a los resultados obtenidos de nuestros servicios.  
•  El Cliente puede publicar los informes solo en forma completa y aclarando quien es el emisor de los mismos. Para su reproducción parcial deberá solicitar autorizacion a Alex Stewart Argentina 

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  podrá usar para fines estadísticos los resultados de los informes de análisis.

•  Escapa a la responsabilidad de Alex Stewart Argentina la evaluación que pueda surgir sobre la aplicación de los resultados emitidos en nuestros Informes de Ensayos.

•  Los informes preliminares previamente emitidos bajo este mismo número de informe quedan reemplazados por el presente informe analítico final.

QA / QC •  Aspectos concernientes a las validaciones metodológicas, sesgo, precisión e incertidumbres asociadas, pueden ser solicitados por el cliente a Alex Stewart Argentina. 
•  Los Límites de cuantificación informados corresponden a los obtenidos en los procesos de validación del método, pueden variar según la matriz y concentración de la muestra.

•  Las Curvas de Calibración empleadas en las metodologías de análisis tienen coeficientes R
2 superiores a 0.99.

•  Se procede a informar solamente los resultados que estén enmarcados dentro del rango de validación o entre el LD y el LCS y a los destinatarios que él explícitamente autorice.                                                                                                                                                

•  Para Au4-30 el Límite de Cuantificación es: LC = 0.06 mg/kg                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              

•  Los valores informados por debajo del LC tienen estadísticamente un grado de confiabilidad menor.

•  Para  lecturas de Cr, Cu, Fe, Mn, Mo y Ni por ICP: Los límites de detección declarados son solo instrumentales, no involucran el tratamiento de la muestra.

CLIENTE: PROYECTOS PASTOS GRANDES S.A. Nº DE COTIZACION: QE-573-3 FECHA RECEPCION DE MUESTRAS: 15/05/2017
DIRECCION: Republica de Israel 131. Salta capital TOTAL DE MUESTRAS: 8 FECHA RECEPCION DE INSTRUCCIONES: 15/05/2017
SOLICITANTE: Silvia Alonso PREPARACION DE MUESTRA: FECHA INGRESO AL LABORATORIO: 15/05/2017

BLANCOS ESTANDARES TIPO DE MUESTRA OTRAS
BL: Blanco de limpieza de cuarzo STD: Standard Pun: puntual Tri: Triplicado N.D : No Detecta ID: Identificación
BK M: Blanco de muestra VN: Valor nominal Dup: Duplicado Rep: Repetición LCS: Límite de cuantificacion superior COD: Código
BK R: Blanco de reactivo SD: Desviación standard Dup C: Duplicado de cuarteo Com: Compuesta LC: Límite de cuantificación LD: Límite de Detección

Muestreo •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace responsable por cualquier aspecto vinculado a las muestras antes de su entrega al laboratorio, en caso de que Alex Stewart  no sea el extractor de las mismas.
•  Los resultados de los análisis de las muestras extraídas por el cliente, pertenecen solo a las muestras en el estado de las mismas al momento de su ingreso a Alex Stewart Argentina  y a partir de la fecha de recepción de las instrucciones.

Almacenaje •  Los rechazos de muestras sólidas recibidas en ASA Argentina serán almacenadas sin costo durante 3 meses. Para muestras líquidas de salmueras al cabo de 45 días de reportadas las muestras se devolverán al cliente a costo de este.
•  Para muestras sólidas, a partir de esa fecha se cobrará el  almacenaje (precios de P-40), salvo que se reciban instrucciones contrarias. 

•  El cliente puede retirar las muestras de nuestras instalaciones o solicitar su eliminación según procedimientos ambientales aceptados a costo al cliente, siendo él responsable absoluto de la disposición final de las muestras devueltas.

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se responsabiliza por alteraciones o daños que naturalmente puedan ocurrirle a las muestras. Las muestras devueltas al clientes carecen de la adición de cualquier substancia o material que atente al medio ambiente.

Informe •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace cargo por el uso que se de a los resultados obtenidos de nuestros servicios.  
•  El Cliente puede publicar los informes solo en forma completa y aclarando quien es el emisor de los mismos. Para su reproducción parcial deberá solicitar autorizacion a Alex Stewart Argentina 

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  podrá usar para fines estadísticos los resultados de los informes de análisis.

•  Escapa a la responsabilidad de Alex Stewart Argentina la evaluación que pueda surgir sobre la aplicación de los resultados emitidos en nuestros Informes de Ensayos.

•  Los informes preliminares previamente emitidos bajo este mismo número de informe quedan reemplazados por el presente informe analítico final.

QA / QC •  Aspectos concernientes a las validaciones metodológicas, sesgo, precisión e incertidumbres asociadas, pueden ser solicitados por el cliente a Alex Stewart Argentina. 
•  Los Límites de cuantificación informados corresponden a los obtenidos en los procesos de validación del método, pueden variar según la matriz y concentración de la muestra.

•  Las Curvas de Calibración empleadas en las metodologías de análisis tienen coeficientes R
2 superiores a 0.99.

•  Se procede a informar solamente los resultados que estén enmarcados dentro del rango de validación o entre el LD y el LCS y a los destinatarios que él explícitamente autorice.                                                                                                                                                

•  Para Au4-30 el Límite de Cuantificación es: LC = 0.06 mg/kg                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              

•  Los valores informados por debajo del LC tienen estadísticamente un grado de confiabilidad menor.

•  Para  lecturas de Cr, Cu, Fe, Mn, Mo y Ni por ICP: Los límites de detección declarados son solo instrumentales, no involucran el tratamiento de la muestra.

BLANCOS ESTANDARES TIPO DE MUESTRA OTRAS
BL: Blanco de limpieza de cuarzo STD: Standard Pun: puntual Tri: Triplicado N.D: No Detecta ID: Identificación
BK M: Blanco de muestra VN: Valor nominal Dup: Duplicado Rep: Repetición LCS: Límite de cuantificacion superior COD: Código
BK R: Blanco de reactivo SD: Desviación standard Dup C: Duplicado de cuarteo Com: Compuesta LC: Límite de cuantificación LD: Límite de Detección

Muestreo •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace responsable por cualquier aspecto vinculado a las muestras antes de su entrega al laboratorio, en caso de que Alex Stewart  no sea el extractor de las mismas.
•  Los resultados de los análisis de las muestras extraídas por el cliente, pertenecen solo a las muestras en el estado de las mismas al momento de su ingreso a Alex Stewart Argentina  y a partir de la fecha de recepción de las instrucciones.

Almacenaje •  Los rechazos de muestras sólidas recibidas en ASA Argentina serán almacenadas sin costo durante 3 meses. Para muestras líquidas de salmueras al cabo de 45 días de reportadas las muestras se devolverán al cliente a costo de este.
•  Para muestras sólidas, a partir de esa fecha se cobrará el  almacenaje (precios de P-40), salvo que se reciban instrucciones contrarias. 

•  El cliente puede retirar las muestras de nuestras instalaciones o solicitar su eliminación según procedimientos ambientales aceptados a costo al cliente, siendo él responsable absoluto de la disposición final de las muestras devueltas.

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se responsabiliza por alteraciones o daños que naturalmente puedan ocurrirle a las muestras. Las muestras devueltas al clientes carecen de la adición de cualquier substancia o material que atente al medio ambiente.

Informe •  Alex Stewart Argentina  no se hace cargo por el uso que se de a los resultados obtenidos de nuestros servicios.  
•  El Cliente puede publicar los informes solo en forma completa y aclarando quien es el emisor de los mismos. Para su reproducción parcial deberá solicitar autorizacion a Alex Stewart Argentina 

•  Alex Stewart Argentina  podrá usar para fines estadísticos los resultados de los informes de análisis.

•  Escapa a la responsabilidad de Alex Stewart Argentina la evaluación que pueda surgir sobre la aplicación de los resultados emitidos en nuestros Informes de Ensayos.

•  Los informes preliminares previamente emitidos bajo este mismo número de informe quedan reemplazados por el presente informe analítico final.

QA / QC •  Aspectos concernientes a las validaciones metodológicas, sesgo, precisión e incertidumbres asociadas, pueden ser solicitados por el cliente a Alex Stewart Argentina. 
•  Los Límites de cuantificación informados corresponden a los obtenidos en los procesos de validación del método, pueden variar según la matriz y concentración de la muestra.

•  Las Curvas de Calibración empleadas en las metodologías de análisis tienen coeficientes R
2 superiores a 0.99.

•  Se procede a informar solamente los resultados que estén enmarcados dentro del rango de validación o entre el LD y el LCS y a los destinatarios que él explícitamente autorice.                                                                                                                                                

•  Para Au4-30 el Límite de Cuantificación es: LC = 0.06 mg/kg                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              

•  Los valores informados por debajo del LC tienen estadísticamente un grado de confiabilidad menor.

•  Para  lecturas de Cr, Cu, Fe, Mn, Mo y Ni por ICP: Los límites de detección declarados son solo instrumentales, no involucran el tratamiento de la muestra.

BL: Blanco de limpieza de cuarzo STD: Standard Pun: puntual Tri: Triplicado N.D : No Detecta ID: Identificación
BK M: Blanco de muestra VN: Valor nominal Dup: Duplicado Rep: Repetición LCS: Límite de cuantificacion superior COD: Código
